Of the treatment of a dislocated shoulder.
Know that the joint of the shoulder and the joint of the muscle do not stretch or dislocate except with such a displacement, and accidents do not occur to them like those that occur to other joints with slight movement and convexity.
And the joint of the shoulder is dislocated in four ways, because it can be dislocated upwards, downwards, forwards, or backwards.
And most often it is dislocated upward, and less often it is dislocated forward or backward.
And the sign of dislocation upwards is that, when you join the arm of the sick person with the healthy one, it becomes longer and the elbow is higher than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their own arm and the place where the elbow would normally be has become swollen from a swelling, therefore the head of the joint is already damaged here.
And the sign that dislocation has occurred in him is that, outwardly, the accidents of it are contrary to this accident. (i.e. The arm is shorter and the elbow is lower than normal)
And the sign that dislocation has occurred in him is that, forwardly, his arm stretches out as far as possible, but he cannot bend it without pain in the elbow, and if he tries to force himself to go on and cannot do so forward; and his urine is retained and his penis is swollen, and you should make him walk on tiptoe.
And the sign that dislocation has occurred in him is that, backwards, he does not stretch out his elbow, nor can he bend it forward as much as he bends his penis; and his arm is shorter than the other, and his penis is softened, and the head of the joint is damaged in that place.
But the reduction of this type of dislocation is that you should consider the hours, if the dislocation is old and ancient, which has already become chronic from being present for a long time, then when you approach him to administer reduction, do not try to reduce it completely; and thus it is not necessary to make any prognosis in such cases.
But in the case of the person who has recently dislocated and is one of the four types of dislocation, at that time you should consider returning the joint to its place and stretching it out both forward and backward, and also from left to right, because it quickly returns to its normal position and does not require further care.
But if it does not return in this manner, then you should prepare strong traction and stretch the arm of him from the most downward part, or from the middle part, or from the upper part where the ligament is attached to the elbow; and another minister should extend the hand of that person so that he can put his fingers into the joints of him; and approach strongly and hold together on the axis of the joint, and have another minister support the extremity of the ligament.

And this type of traction is common to all four types. (This suggests that the method of traction described is applicable to all four types of dislocation mentioned earlier)
And therefore, if the dislocation returns to its normal position as we have said, then it is well; and otherwise, it is necessary for each type of traction that I will say about proper treatment. The treatment of a dislocated ankle.
The ankle sometimes is put back in place with a small force, and sometimes it is dislocated according to its structure, and the dislocation of it is done either from behind or from in front.
